<s> the dining room after lunch <\s>
<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> the dining room after lunch <\s>
<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>

<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>

<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>

<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>
<s> johnny sits on the fender smoking a cigarette and warming his back <\s>
<s> he is a commonplace looking young man with a decided jaw tall neat soulful who has been in the war and writes poetry <\s>
<s> mary is less ordinary you cannot tell exactly what is the matter with her <\s>
<s> she too is tall a little absent fair and well looking <\s>
<s> she has a small china dog in her hand taken from the mantelpiece and faces the audience <\s>
<s> as the curtain rises she is saying in her soft and pleasant voice well what is the matter with us all johnny <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>

<s> thursday a fortnight later <\s>
<s> the dining room after lunch <\s>
<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>
<s> johnny sits on the fender smoking a cigarette and warming his back <\s>
<s> he is a commonplace looking young man with a decided jaw tall neat soulful who has been in the war and writes poetry <\s>
<s> mary is less ordinary you cannot tell exactly what is the matter with her <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>

<s> the dining room after lunch <\s>
<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>
<s> johnny sits on the fender smoking a cigarette and warming his back <\s>
<s> he is a commonplace looking young man with a decided jaw tall neat soulful who has been in the war and writes poetry <\s>
<s> mary is less ordinary you cannot tell exactly what is the matter with her <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> the dining room after lunch <\s>
<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>

<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>

<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>

<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>
<s> mrs march still sits behind the coffee pot making up her daily list on tablets with a little gold pencil fastened to her wrist <\s>
<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>
<s> mr march is sitting in an armchair sideways to the windows smoking his pipe and reading his newspaper with little explosions to which no one pays any attention because it is his daily habit <\s>
<s> he is a fine looking man of fifty odd with red grey moustaches and hair both of which stiver partly by nature and partly because his hands often push them up <\s>
<s> mary and johnny are close to the fireplace stage right <\s>
<s> johnny sits on the fender smoking a cigarette and warming his back <\s>
<s> he is a commonplace looking young man with a decided jaw tall neat soulful who has been in the war and writes poetry <\s>
<s> mary is less ordinary you cannot tell exactly what is the matter with her <\s>
<s> she too is tall a little absent fair and well looking <\s>
<s> she has a small china dog in her hand taken from the mantelpiece and faces the audience <\s>
<s> as the curtain rises she is saying in her soft and pleasant voice well what is the matter with us all johnny <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>
<s> a hammock under the acacias shows that mary lies there sometimes with her eyes on the gleam of sunlight that comes through and a trail in the longish grass bordered with cigarette ends proves that johnny tramps there with his eyes on the ground or the stars according <\s>
<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
<s> the marches have been at breakfast and the round table covered with blue linen is thick with remains seven baskets full <\s>
<s> the room is gifted with old oak furniture there is a door stage left forward a hearth where a fire is burning and a high fender on which one can sit stage right middle and in the wall below the fireplace a service hatch covered with a sliding shutter for the passage of dishes into the adjoining pantry <\s>
<s> against the wall stage left is an old oak dresser and a small writing table across the left back corner <\s>

<s> she is personable forty eight trim well dressed and more matter of fact than seems plausible <\s>

<s> act i the march's dining room opens through french windows on one of those gardens which seem infinite till they are seen to be coterminous with the side walls of the house and finite at the far end because only the thick screen of acacias and sumachs prevents another house from being seen <\s>
<s> the french and other windows form practically all the outer wall of that dining room and between them and the screen of trees lies the difference between the characters of mr and mrs march with dots and dashes of mary and johnny thrown in <\s>
<s> for instance it has been formalised by mrs march but the grass has not been cut by mr march and daffodils have sprung up there which mrs march desires for the dining room but of which mr march says for god's sake joan let them grow <\s>
<s> about half therefore are now in a bowl on the breakfast table and the other half still in the grass in the compromise essential to lasting domesticity <\s>

<s> but all this is by the way because except for a yard or two of gravel terrace outside the windows it is all painted on the backcloth <\s>
